Jamison Brereton

121
Indra or the All Gods
Kakс╣г─лvant Dairghatamasa
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Of all the challenging and maddening hymns in Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs small but memorable oeuvre, this hymn may present the biggest challenges and the most maddening set of puzzlesтАФthough the immediately preceding one is at least in competition. It seems that antiquity had a similar reaction, as the Anukramaс╣З─л is not even sure whether the hymn is dedicated to Indra or to the All Gods. We will here sketch a structure and suggest some themes, but we make no claims for the correctness of all the choices made in our translation or commentary.
The predominant deity of the hymn must be Indra, though his name does not appear until verse 11, and the governing myth of the hymn is that of the opening of the Vala cave. But other mythic material is interspersed through the hymn, and the present-day sacrificial situation is also treatedтАФwhile, conversely, the Vala myth is sometimes presented as if it were happening at this moment. In fact, the first verse sets up this scenario, with questions about IndraтАЩs attendance at a sacrifice where the Aс╣Еgirases, his helpers in the Vala myth, are performing their hymns. The same prospective appearance of Indra among the Aс╣Еgirases is also described in verse 3, with the recital of the Vala myth continued, in the past, in verse 4. The intervening verse (2) is also couched in the mythic past and begins (2ab) with IndraтАЩs primal cosmogonic deed, the separation of heaven and earth. The second half of verse 2 contains one of the most discussed portions of the hymn, a set of three memorably described female figures whose relationships to each other and to the тАЬbuffaloтАЭ who is gazing upon at least one of them are unclear. In our view, all three figures are different forms of Dawn, the subject of two of Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs other hymns (I.123тАУ124), as she transforms herself from a young girl choosing her husband (the Sun) to a wife (of the Sun in the form of a horse) to a mother (of a cow: the light of Dawn is frequently compared to cows). The buffalo is probably Indra, and the focus on Dawn is appropri ate to a hymn celebrating the opening of the Vala cave and the release of the dawn-cows.
Verse 4 alluded to the impetus that drinking soma gave to Indra at the opening of the Vala cave, and the following two verses (5тАУ6) sketch the history of IndraтАЩs possession of soma and then turn to the soma currently being produced at todayтАЩs dawn sacrifice. The following, quite puzzling verse (7) seems to identify Indra with the sun and, by implication, with the shining soma of the previous verse, also com
pared to the sun. The poet seems further to suggest that, even in the absence of all the sacrificial necessities, the presence of radiant Indra is tantamount to a properly performed sacrifice, for the benefit of the poet and his family. (We suggest that Kakс╣г─лvant is alluding to himself here, on the basis of similar vocabulary used in I.126.5.)
Verse 8 begins a series of mythological verses, with an intertwining of the Vala myth (9ab, 10ab) and that of IndraтАЩs slaying of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa with the aid of U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya (9cd, 10cd, 11d, 12) and the related myth of the halting of the SunтАЩs horses and chariot (13), with incidental mentions of other deeds of Indra (the Vr╠еtra battle, 11c) thrown in. The interpenetration of these mythic allusions keeps the audi
ence off balance, a queasy feeling much increased by the disjunctive and elliptical syntax.

The final two verses (14тАУ15), asking for protection and valuables, are by contrast quite straightforward. Presumably on this subject Kakс╣г─лvant did not want the god to misunderstand.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra or the All Gods This is a very problematic hymn, and both the published translation and this comm. are tentative and tenuous on many points. There are some quirks that reappear throughout the hymn: a remarkable no. of p─Бda-final g├│с╕е (2b, 2d, 7b, 9a) - is this some sort of hidden encoding? ItтАЩs also part of a pattern of favoring p─Бda-final monosyllables (vr─Б╠Бm 2c, r─Б╠Бс╣н 3a, dy┼л╠Бn 3b, 7c, dy─Б╠Бm 3d, vaс╕е 4d, nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn 12a, 13a, d─Б╠Бt 12c

  • and, flg. Hoffmann, daс╕е 10d). Also a fondness for p├бri and pr├б, the former esp. in opaque contexts.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen willIndra, the protector of men and granter of riches, listen to the praises thus (recited) of the Aс╣Еgirasas, who are devoted to the gods? When he perceives the ministers of the master of the mansion, and is to be the object of worship in the sacrifice, he greatly exults.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Will he, hastening to the cup of the men seeking the gods, listen properly to the hymns of the Aс╣Еgirases?
When he has reached the clans of the secure habitation, will the one worthy of the sacrifice stride widely at their ceremony?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take p─Бda a as a separate clause and consider p─Б╠Бtram тАШcup, vesselтАЩ a metaphorical designation of Indra (тАЬIst er wohl das rechte Gef├дss f├╝r solch gottergebene M├дnner?тАЭ). With Oldenberg I consider this to be an anachronistic application of the much later sense of тАШcup, bowlтАЩ to mean тАШappropriate recipientтАЩ. (It is true that Indra is referred to as a тАШtankardтАЩ [I.61.9] and a тАШbeakerтАЩ [I.100.12] elsewhere, but in those cases it is his capacious size that is at issue.) Oldenberg and Renou both avoid the Indra = cup interpretation by supplying a verb (different verbs in each case). I see no reason to supply a verb, since p─Б╠Бtram can be an acc. goal with turaс╣Зy├бn (see X.61.11 for another acc. of goal with the same stem), a possibility also allowed by Oldenberg

On nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn as gen. pl. see AiG III.211-12.

Griffith

WHEN Will men’s guardians hasting hear with favour the song of Angiras’s pious
children?
When to the people of the home he cometh he strideth to the sacrifice, the Holy.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe verily upholds the heaven; he, the brilliant, the leader of the (stolen) herd, pours forth the flowing (water), for the sake of food; the mighty Indra manifests himself after his own daughter (the dawn); he made the feminine le of the horse unnaturally the mother of the cow.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra = the sun. In jest (?), Indra is said to have made a mare bring forth a calf

Jamison Brereton

He propped up heaven, and he sprinkled its foundation [=earth]. The ingenious one (provided) movable wealth of man and cow for the prize. The buffalo gazed after (Dawn,) the self-created maiden making her choice (of husband), (who turned into) the consort of the horse
[=Sun], (then into) the mother of the cow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take n├бro as the nom. sg. of a thematic form of the тАШmanтАЩ stem, a nom. sg. that is otherwise not found in the RV (save possibly in sv├аrс╣Зara-) and only very sparingly in the rest of Vedic (see AiG III.212). I follow Grassmann, Oldenberg, and Witzel Got┼Н in taking it as a gen. sg. of the athematic тАШmanтАЩ stem, even though the other two occurrences registered by Grassmann are better taken as nom. pl. It replaces expected *nur (cf. Aves. n╔Щr╔Щ┼б). It is parallel here to g├│с╕е, and this gen. expression characterizes the type of dr├бviс╣Зa- that Indra is providing as a prize. Since dr├бviс╣Зa- is a derivative of тИЪdru тАШrunтАЩ, it really is тАШmoveable wealthтАЩ, and both cattle and men would qualify.

The pair n├бro g├│с╕е is echoed by the more conventional expression c├бtuс╣гpade тАж dvip─Б╠Бde in 3d, which also contains the qualifier n├бry─Бya.

The opening с╣Ыbh├║r v─Б╠Бj─Бya contains the names of two of the three с╣Ъbhus, though the words are not so used here.

As indicated in the published introduction, the second hemistich is much discussed, and I will not treat other interpretations in detail. It depicts a buffalo (mahiс╣г├б-) gazing after (and probably longing after) three females, or, in my interpr., one female in three different shapes. These shapes are three standard female roles, arranged chronologically: marriageable girl (according to my interpr. of vr─Б╠Б- as тАШchooserтАЩ; see comm. VIII.2.6), wife/consort (m├йn─Б- тЖР тАШexchange tokenтАЩ; see comm. I.62.7), and mother. The mahiс╣г├б- is Indra, as often; this word also evokes the term for the chief wife of a king, m├бhiс╣г─л-, thus indirectly adding another female role. I identify the female referent of all three as Dawn. Kakс╣г─лvant calls Dawn тАЬbegetter of cowsтАЭ (g├бv─Бс╣Г j├бnitr─л) in nearby I.124.5, like our m─Бt├бraс╣Г g├│с╕е, and also compares her to a vr─Б╠Б- in I.124.8. Since Dawn is always depicted in motion, тАЬgaze after (a retreating figure)тАЭ is an appropriate verb. (Cf. IV.18.3 where Indra anu тИЪcakс╣г his mother who is going away: par─Бyat─л╠Бm m─Бt├бram ├бnv acaс╣гс╣нa.) If the referent is Dawn, then the horse whose consort she is is probably the sun. For Dawn and the horse = sun, see VII.77.3.

The term svaj─Б╠Б- тАШself-createdтАЩ has two applications in the passage. On the one hand, it characterizes the vr─Б╠Б- particularly. Since she is a тАШchooserтАЩ, the female protagonist of a svayaс╣Гvara (self-choice) marriage, she is тАШself-createdтАЩ because she is not being given to someone by someone else, but is doing it herself. If marriage is the equivalent of upanayana and second birth for women, then sheтАЩs her own parent.

On the other hand, it can characterize all the role transformations she undergoes in cd, loosely тАЬ(re)creating herself as тАжтАЭ For further on vr─Б╠Б- and this passage in general, see Jamison 2003 (Fs. H.-P. Schmidt) pp. 45-47, also X.111.3.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay he, illuminating the purple (dawn), listen to the invocation (addressed to him) of old, daily besowing wealth upon the race of Aс╣Еgiras; he has sharpened his fatal shaft; he has supported the heaven for the good of men, of quadrupeds, andbipeds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The surpassing king will come through the days to the age-old call of the clans of the Aс╣Еgirases for the ruddy (cows).
He will fashion the mace, his team-mate; he will prop up heaven for the sake of the two-footed and four-footed belonging to men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation this verse is couched in the English future because I took two of the three verbs in the verse (n├бkс╣гat and tast├бmbhat) as subjunctives and the third (t├бkс╣гat) as an injunctive but a rhyme form to n├бkс╣гat, each of them beginning a hemistich. I considered the verse a continuation of the prospective questions in vs. 1.

about IndraтАЩs coming to the sacrifice. I have now accepted the view of Narten (Sig.Aor. 160; see also Hoffmann Injunk. 144) that n├бkс╣гat is instead an injunctive to the thematic stem of the enlarged root тИЪnakс╣г. This then seems to strand tast├бmbhat as a lone subjunctive in this sequence; K├╝mmel (575) labels it a subjunctive in preterital context. However, the passage may originally have had the indic. pf. *tast├бmbha, and tasth├бmbhat may have picked up a final dental from the initial of the following word: tast├бmbhad dy─Б╠Бm# to match preceding n├бkс╣гat and t├бkс╣гat. Since dy─Б╠Бm begins with a cluster, the meter is unaffected by a reading *tast├бmbha dy─Б╠Бm. The cadence is terrible (four heavy syllables), but the only thing that would improve it is reading

*tastabha(d), with a zero-grade root syllable appropriate neither to the indicative nor to the subjunctive.

Revising my understanding of the morphology requires revising the translation as well. I would now take the whole verse in the past: тАЬThe surpassing king came through the days to the age-old call of the clans of the Aс╣Еgirases for the ruddy (cows). He fashioned the mace, his team-mate; he propped up heaven for the sake of the two-footed and four-footed belonging to men.тАЭ The verse then provides a reassuring model in the past for IndraтАЩs hoped-for activity in the present. Note that n├бkс╣гat picks up the aor. ─Б╠Бnaс╣н (approximately) from 1c and tast├бmbha(t) the aor.

st├бmbh─лt of 2a.

Geldner takes aruс╣З─л╠Бс╕е as nom. sg. fem., appositive to r─Б╠Бс╣н, which must then be fem.

and mean тАШqueenтАЩ (тАЬdie Morgenr├╢te, die K├╢niginтАЭ). Both of these are grammatically possible: r─Б╠Бс╣н must be fem. in V.46.8; aruс╣З─л╠Бс╕е must be nom. sg. in IV.1.16, 14.3. But this leaves the apparent masc. nom. sg. adj. tur├бс╕е without a head. I therefore take aruс╣З─л╠Бс╕е as acc. pl., loosely construed with h├бvam. See Oldenberg The ruddy ones are presumably the cows imprisoned in the Vala cave, who reappear (with a different color term, usr├нya-) in vs. 4.

Griffith

Lord of red dawns, he came victorious, daily to the Angirases’ former invocation.
His bolt and team hath he prepared, and stablished the heaven for quadrupeds and men two-footed.

Geldner

Es kam auf den Ruf zuerst die Morgenr├╢te, die K├╢nigin; es kam auf den Ruf der Angiras┬┤ der Gebieter der Clane alle Tage. Er zimmerte die ihm zu eigen gegebene Keule; er st├╝tzte den Himmel f├╝r die den Herren geh├╢rigen Vierf├╝├Яler und Zweif├╝├Яler.

Grassmann

Es vernahm das Gebr├╝ll der r├╢thlichen [? im Gew├╢lk eingeschlossenen] Kuh der starke Gebieter der Menschen und der Angira’s Tag f├╝r Tag; er machte zurecht den Blitz und das Gespann, befestigte den Himmel dem vierf├╝ssigen Geschlecht und dem zweif├╝ssigen der Menschen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIn the exhilaration of the Soma, you have restored the celebrated herd of cattle, hidden (in the cave), for the sake of sacrifice, (to the Aс╣Еgirasas); when, Indra, the threefold crest engages in combat, he opens the doors of the tyrannical descendants of ManuтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Threefold crest: elevated as a triple crest in the three worlds

Jamison Brereton

In the exhilaration of this (soma) you gave the noisy vanguard of the ruddy (cows), (previously) covered over, to truth,
when the three-humped (herd) was (momentarily) turned back in its forward surge. You uncovered the deceits and unclosed the doors for the (people) descended from Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Unlike the standard tr. I take c with ab rather than with d. I also take the subject of that p─Бda, the referent of trikak├║b тАШthree-humpedтАЩ, as the herd, not Indra with most tr. The problem is the verb, niv├бrtat. On the surface it is the only active form to the quite well-attested them. pres. v├бrtate. It could be taken as an oppositional transitive active built (however temporarily) to the intransitive middle.

Since n├н тИЪvс╣Ыt generally means тАШturn backтАЩ (of bovines), it could mean тАШ(make) turn backтАЩ, with Indra as subject (called trikak├║b). The problem is that this doesnтАЩt make a lot of sense in context. He has just released them (or so I take ab); why then at their тАЬforward surgeтАЭ (pras├бrge) would he make them reverse direction? What I think the p─Бda depicts is the cows milling around in cow-like fashion and beginning to move, but something stops or confuses them, turning them back (p─Бda c), and Indra has to step in and show them the way out (p─Бdas ab, d). A (partial) solution to this difficulty was seen by Hoffmann (Aufs. II, 590), who identifies several forms as belonging to an intransitive root aorist to тИЪvс╣Ыt, to which this would be the subjunctive, rather than belonging to the them. pres. stem. Since the forms are intransitive, this solves my valency problem, but the subjunctive causes some difficulties. Hoffman takes p─Бda c as a purpose clause тАЬDamit er beim Losrennen (der K├╝he) als Spitzentier zur├╝ckkehre,тАЭ but why, again, would Indra turn back? To make it fit my scenario, with the herd as subject, I need to read it as a past prospective. Indra got them on the way to truth when they were going to / would have turned back. I would slightly amend my tr. to тАЬwhen the three-humped (herd) was going to turn back in its forward surge.тАЭ There is another possible conceptual solution, also utilizing HoffmannтАЩs intransitive root aorist subjunctive. As already noted, n├н тИЪvс╣Ыt means тАШturn backтАЩ of bovines – see the extraordinary concentration of this lexeme in X.19, a hymn urging the cows to return. If we assume that once the cows trapped in the Vala cave are released, they will return home (which would be expressed by n├н тИЪvrс╣н), then niv├бrtat is compatible with pras├бrge: тАЬso that the three-humped (herd) will return (home) in its forward surge.тАЭ In d I take ├бpa тАж vaс╕е in two slightly different senses with two different objects: тАШuncoverтАЩ with dr├║haс╕е тАШdeceitsтАЩ and тАШuncloseтАЩ (= тАШopenтАЩ) with d├║raс╕е тАШdoorsтАЩ (note the phonological similarity of the two objects). Unlike many tr. I therefore do not take dr├║haс╕е as gen. dependent on d├║raс╕е; I also consider m─Б╠Бnuс╣гasya as a gen. of benefit rather than construing it with dr├║haс╕е (for both, cf. RenouтАЩs тАЬles portes du Mal humainтАЭ).

Griffith

In joy of this thou didst restore, for worship, the lowing company of hidden cattle.
When the three-pointed one descends with onslaught he opens wide the doors that cause man trouble.

Geldner

Im Rausche dieses Soma gabst du die eingeschlossene l├дrmende Reihe der K├╝he der Rechtm├д├Яigkeit zur├╝ck. Als der Dreispitz sie im Zuge zur├╝ckf├╝hrte, da schlo├Я er die Tore auf, die Betr├╝ger des Menschen.

Grassmann

In seinem Rausche verhalf er der eingeschlossenen rauschenden Schar der K├╝he zu ihrem Rechte, als er bei seinem Vordringen den mit drei Spitzen versehenen Blitz niederschleuderte und die Th├╝ren des menschen├дhnlichen Unholdes [des Vritra] erbrach.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen your parents, (heaven and earth), theprotectors (of the world), brought the nutritious and invigorating oblation to you, who are quick in act, and when they offered you the pure and precious milk of the cow.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The cow: i.e. the clarified butter of the oblations, from which the nutriment of all things proceeds, for the oblation ascends to the sun, by whom rain is engendered, from which springs corn, the support of living beings; when this has beendone, Indra opens the doors of the cave, and rescues the cattle, as described in the preceding verse, with which this is connected

Jamison Brereton

For you is this milk, consisting of good semen, which your two bustling parents brought as a bounty, (for you) to become surpassingтАФ
your blazing legacy, which they gained through sacrifice, the milk of the ruddy one who gives sap as milk.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Under this elaborate disguise, the verse is simply about soma and IndraтАЩs possession of it. The parents are, acdg. to most, Heaven and Earth.

Griffith

Thine is that milk which thy swift-moving Parents brought down, a strengthening genial gift for conquest;
When the pure treasure unto thee they offered, the milk shed from the cow who streameth nectar.

Geldner

F├╝r dich war die Milch, die beide Eltern eilig brachten, die Gabe aus gutem Samen dir zum Sieg, der reine Trank, den sie dir als dein Eigentum zum Opfer brachten, die Milch der immermelken Kuh.

Grassmann

Als dir die Aeltern [Himmel und Erde] die Milch darreichten als segensreiche Gabe, die gesch├дftigen, eilenden, und als dir die Opferer die Milch der Nektar str├╢menden Kuh als gl├дnzendes Erbtheil brachten,

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNow is Indra manifested; may he, the over-comer (of his foes), grant us happiness,he, who shines brightly, like the sun of this dawn; may the excellent Soma, being sprinklled upon the plural ceof sacrifice with a ladle, (exhilarate us), by whom, presenting the oblations we had prepared, it was imbibed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And now he [=Soma] has been producedтАФlet him give exhilaration as he advances; he has shone forth like the sun from this dawn,
when the drop, (being impelled) by (priests) having sweat as their
oblation, (itself) pouring with the offering spoon, has reached its old (ritual) domains.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another verse about soma.

Note the position of n├б in the simile, where it is placed after the two-word DET+NOUN phrase (asy─Б╠Бuс╣г├бsaс╕е) rather than after the first word. I do not know if this placement is by rule; it might be worth looking for other examples with this configuration. In fact, see I.129.1g with im─Б╠Бс╣Г v─Б╠Бcaс╣Г n├б.

The syntax is somewhat clotted in the 2nd hemistich. With Geldner I take y├йbhiс╕е as standing for *y├бd ebh├нс╕е vel sim., since there is no masc. pl. referent in the main clause. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and Renou construe the instr. without further verbal support (Geldner тАЬmit Hilfe der ihren Schweiss opfernden (Priester)тАЭ). I supply тАШbeing impelledтАЩ to account for the instr.; such expressions are relatively common in soma hymns; cf. IX.30.2 = 107.26 ├нndur hiy─Бn├бс╕е sotс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е, etc. For sweat as an oblation, see Jamison 2015 (тАЬAvestan xс╣г╠Мuu─лd-: A Relic of Indo-Iranian Ritual Vocabulary,тАЭ BAI 25).

The si├▒c├бn of d causes some conceptual problems. Active forms of this very common stem are transitive (тАШpour xтАЩ), but if the subject remains the drop (├нnduс╕е), a passive тАШbeing pouredтАЩ would seem to make more sense. However, this attribution of agency to the drop – to pour himself, as it were – fits with the general tendency to animatize soma and attribute exceptional powers to him.

Witzel Got┼Н take jar├бс╣З─Б as a nom. sg. fem., an abstract тАЬLanglebigkeit,тАЭ conceived of as a goddess, as opposed to its standard interpr. as a neut. pl. adj. modifying dh─Б╠Бma and essentially identical to differently accented jaraс╣З├б- тАШoldтАЩ (Geldner, Renou, though not Grassmann).

For Witzel Got┼Н this goddess is the one who pours with the spoon and reaches the seat. This is clever but runs into difficulties. First, forms to тИЪjс╣Ы generally convey a negative sense of тАШageтАЩ – not тАШlong lifeтАЩ. And it interferes with a standard soma trope, of the pressed soma going to / reaching his тАЬdomains,тАЭ which is straightforwardly present here as long as ├нnduс╕е remains the subject. And as far as I know, there is no other evidence for this goddess.

Griffith

There is he born. May the Swift give us rapture, and like the Sun shine forth from yonder dawning,
Indu, even us who drank, whose toils are offerings, poured from the spoon, with praise, upon the altar.

Geldner

Nun ist er geboren; erfolgreich soll er berauschen. Er leuchte hervor wie die Sonne aus dieser Morgenr├╢te, wenn der Saft mit Hilfe der ihren Schwei├Я opfernden Priester, mit der Kelle eingie├Яend, in die alten Gef├д├Яe gelangt ist.

Grassmann

Da ward der Indusaft erzeugt, der vordringende berausche dich; er ergl├дnzte wie dieses Morgens Sonne, als er durch die im Schweisse opfernden aus der Somakelle mit Rauschen str├╢mend zu dem Sitze [der Opferstreu] gelangte,

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the bright-edged hatchet is ready for its work, the directing priest is able to have the victim bound in the sacrifice; when Indra, you shine upon the days that are appropriated to sacred rites, then (success attends) upon the man who goes with his cart (for fuel), the driver (of cattle), or the active (shepherd).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hatchet: vanadhiti, the weapon used to cut down the trees in the forest; pari rodhan─Б goс╕е: the phrase has no verb; it is explained as: pasvi rodhan─Бya yupe niyoj─Бya, pari samartho bhavati, the priest, the adhvaryu, is competent for the attachment of the animal to the stake. Alternative: vanadhiti = a collection of water (goс╕е = water or rain;

Vana = megham─Бl─Б, body of clouds, ready to rain); hence, Indra in the firmament is able to remove any impediment to the shower. Upon the man who goes: anarvi┼Ыe pa┼Ыviс╣гe tur─Бya = to the cartman to the cattle-driver, to the quick; explained as: abhimatam sidhyet = his wish may succeed;

Anarvi┼Ыe = cartman, ‘he who goes to fetch fuel from the wood, in his cart’;

Pa┼Ыviс╣гe = the driver of cattle;

Tur─Бya = active or quick;

Gop─Бla = shepherd

Jamison Brereton

(Even) when a woodpile provided with good kindling should be far away, the sun (still goes) around the cowpens at the ceremony,
when you [=Indra] shine forth, through the days that bring results, for the surpassing one [=Kakс╣г─лvant?] whose clan is on the (wedding?)
carts, seeking livestock.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another very obscure verse with multiple competing interpretations. I will only discuss my own. As indicated in the published introduction. I think the larger point of the verse is that IndraтАЩs presence alone is sufficient for an effective sacrifice, even if the standard ritual trappings (like the wood for the fire) are absent. This rests in part on very different interpr. of the individual lexical items, esp. in p─Бda a.

To start there, the hapax van├бdhiti- is interpr. by Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н), Scarlatta (57), going back to S─Бyaс╣Зa, as an axe, the Holzmacherin, in part because of the phonological play with a standard word for тАШaxeтАЩ sv├бdhiti-. I follow Grassmann (Oldenberg, Renou, Schmidt Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 147) in taking it rather as the pile of wood for the kindling of the ritual fire, formed like v├бsu-dhiti- тАШtreasure chamber, depository of goodsтАЩ; cf. also mitr├б-dhiti- in the adjacent hymn (I.120.9). The verb in this clause, apasy─Б╠Бt, is universally considered a subjunctive to a denom. stem apas-y├б- тАШbe activeтАЩ (a stem that would appear only here, though there are related nominal forms); I interpret it rather as the optative of ├бpa тИЪas тАШbeтАЩ (hence apa-sy─Б╠Бt) тАШbe away, be distantтАЩ. True, this lexeme is not common – I have found only one other RVic example (X.83.5) – but it would be easy to create, with additive semantics, and semantically parallel ├бpa тИЪbh┼л is better established.

There is no agreement on the sense of p─Бda b or even its syntactic status: because it lacks an overt verb, it is not clear whether it continues the subordinate clause of p─Бda or functions as the main clause. (With Geldner et al., I assume it is the main clause, since otherwise the verse consists only of subordinate clauses.) It is generally assumed that a finite verb should be supplied with p├бri; I supply the inoffensive тАШgoтАЩ.

My interpr. of the p─Бda is, on the other hand, rather bold – there seems no other choice with p─Бdas like these. I take the cowpens (r├│dhan─Б g├│с╕е) as a reference to the ritual ground or to the vessels containing the milk to be mixed with soma or perhaps to places where animals are kept for sacrifice. The тАЬsunтАЭ that goes around them is either Agni performing the paryagnikaraс╣Зa, the circling around ritual objects or sacrificial animals (the latter might make more sense with cowpens), or Soma circling through the purifying filter. Both Agni and Soma are frequently identified with the sun.

But the mediating image for p─Бda b is the radiant Indra of p─Бda c. When Indra (such is my identification of the subj. of the 2nd sg. prabh─Б╠Бsi) shines forth, there is no need of wood for the fire (p─Бda a). He can stand in for the ritual fire and/or the gleaming soma and bring the sacrifice to a successful conclusion by himself, as it were.

My identification of Indra as the subj. of c makes him unavailable to be the referent of the datives in d, as Geldner, Renou take them. In my view, the poet Kakс╣г─лvant is a better candidate (see Witzel Got┼Н, who suggest тАЬSippenf├╝hrer,тАЭ so at least not a god). For one thing, if the curious hapax cmpd ├бnarvi┼Ы- contains the (pseudo-)loc. ├бnar- to ├бnas- тАШcartтАЩ, it seems unlikely that this would qualify anyone directly associated with Indra – the cart is not a warriorтАЩs vehicle – while on the other hand the Pajras, Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs clan (cf., e.g., I.116.7, 117.6), are ├бnasvant- тАШpossessing carts / wagonsтАЩ (or, more accurately, compared to people who are ├бnasvant-) in I.126.5. Although tur├б- was used of Indra in 3b and would here be applied to Kakс╣г─лvant, this poet would surely not mind getting a little reflected divine glory. Note, in passing, the phonetic echo in ├бnarvi┼Ыe pa┼Ы u viс╣гe.

Griffith

When the wood-pile, made of good logs, is ready, at the Sun’s worship to bind fast the Bullock,
Then when thou shinest forth through days of action for the Car-borne, the Swift, the Cattle-seeker.

Geldner

Wenn die Holzmacherin, die gutes Brennholz hat, t├дtig sein wird, so soll w├дhrend des Opfers die Sonne das Gef├дngnis der Kuh ├╝berwinden, wenn du hervorleuchtest w├дhrend der entscheidenden Tage f├╝r den Gebieter, der mit seinem auf Karren fahrenden Clan die Herde sucht.

Grassmann

Wenn der mit gutem Brennholz versehene Holzstoss in Wirksamkeit tritt, als Sonne beim Opfer strahlend um den Verschluss des Rindes (?), und wenn du [Agni?] dann leuchtest in den festlichen (?) Tagen dem im Wagen fahrenden, Vieh [Milch] begehrenden, starken [Indra?].

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSend hither your horses, the quaffers of the exhilarating libation; overcome, warrior, the adversary plural ndering us of our treasure; when they express with stones, for the increase (of your strength), the delightful, exhilarating, invigorating (Soma), to be overtaken by you, who are swifter than the wind.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You brought here the two tawny (horses) attained from great heaven, as you were battling for the wellspring (of soma), which was
overwhelming in heavenly brilliance,
when for you to grow strong they milked with stones the exhilarating tawny (soma), that was frenzied for cows [=milk], befriended by
the wind.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The major puzzle in this verse is the grammatical identity of its first word, aс╣гс╣н─Б╠Б. Geldner takes as the agent noun to тИЪa┼Ы тАШattainтАЩ, which is not otherwise attested (and for which we should expect full grade *naс╣гс╣н├бr-), while Oldenberg, Renou, Scarlatta (602), Witzel Got┼Н take it as тАШeightтАЩ (which of course requires some clever manoeuvering with its head noun, dual h├бr─л). I follow S─Бyaс╣Зa, Grassmann in taking it as the ppl. to тИЪ(n)a┼Ы.

On the sense of v─Бt─Б╠Бpya- see comm. ad IX.93.5. The scansion of this stem is unclear: Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition give it as v─Б╠Гt─Б╠Бpyam, that is, presumably, v─Бat─Б╠Бpyam, Arnold (p. 294) vaat─Б╠Бpyam (with short first vowel), but Oldenberg v─Бta─Б╠Бpyam. Ad IX.93.5 he also suggests v─Бt─Б╠Бpiyam (which wouldnтАЩt work here), pronouncing the scansion favored by Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition the least likely. Grassmann also goes for -piya-.

I.121.9-13: Hoffmann (Inj. 191 and n. 157) transl. and comments on these mythological verses.

Griffith

Eight steeds thou broughtest down from mighty heaven, when fighting for the well that giveth splendour,
That men might press with stones the gladdening yellow, strengthened with milk, fermenting, to exalt thee.

Vom hohen Himmel nahmst du dir die Rosse, erk├дmpftest hier den Kraft verleihnden Brunnen, Dass man mit Steinen dir den goldnen Rauschtrank zur Lust den starken milchgemischten melke.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou did hurl your metal bolt upon the quick-moving (asura), the swift destroyer of foes, that was brought (to you) by с╣Ъbhu from heaven; when you, who are worshipped by many, striking ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, for the sake of Kutsa, did encompass him with numberless fatal (weapons).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Brought by с╣Ъbhu from heaven: divo ─Бn─лtam с╣Ъbhv─Б;

с╣Ъbhu = Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, fabricator of Indra’s thunderbolt. ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa = drought; Indra removes drought for the benefit of his worshippers,by many drops of rain

Jamison Brereton

Ingenious, you rolled back from the cow the metallic stone of heaven, which had been brought nearby,
when, o much-invoked one, vanquishing ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, you kept encircling him with endless deadly weapons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The puzzle in this verse is what is happening to the cow (g├│с╕е) – which depends on what case the word is in and on the interpretation of the VP pr├бti vartayaс╕е тАж ├б┼Ыm─Бnam. If the VP is taken as hostile (тАЬturn the stone against XтАЭ), g├│с╕е is difficult to fit in, since as a gen.-abl. it canтАЩt easily be a target. See the standard tr., plus Hoffmann (Inj. 191), for various attempts to wrestle with this possibility.

However, the VP can instead mean тАЬroll the stone back,тАЭ with g├│с╕е an ablative тАЬfrom the cowтАЭ and the action depicted a friendly and helpful one. I consider this to be a variant of the Vala myth, referring to the opening of the cave. The problem is that the Vala myth does not ordinarily intersect with the ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa story, which occupies the 2nd hemistich, but, as indicated in the published introduction, the two myths are woven together in this part of the hymn.

Another problem is the present tense pariy─Б╠Бsi of d, in a hymn otherwise couched in the mythological past. In conjunction with anant├б- тАШendlessтАЩ, I suggest that the present is used here to express a past continuative тАШkept XingтАЩ.

Griffith

Thou hurledst forth from heaven the iron missile, brought by the Skilful, from the sling of leather,
When thou, O Much-invoked, assisting Kutsa with endless deadly darts didst compass Susna.

Du kehrtest geschickt den dargereichten ehernen Spie├Я der Kuh in den Himmelskeil um, wobei du Vielgerufener f├╝r Kutsa Partei nehmend den Susna mit endlosen Streichen einholest.

Du schleudertest den eisernen, von Ribhu geschenkten Keil des Himmels aus dem Riemen, Als, vielgerufner, du dem Kutsa helfend mit Hieben ohne Zahl den ├Зuschna anfielst.

When it is just before the sun enters into (the fold) of darkness, then cast the missile against the bolt, o possessor of the stones.
Even the power of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa that surrounded himтАФthat you tore away from heaven, even though it was well-knotted.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sequence of tense/mood in this verse is somewhat puzzling, with an impv. in the first hemistich (asya, p─Бda b) followed by a 2nd sg. impf. (─Б╠Б-adar, so Pp.) or injunctive (─Б╠Б-dar, so Hoffmann, Inj. 191). This discrepancy must be why Geldner puts the first hemistich in quotation marks, though he doesnтАЩt explain who is speaking.

In my opinion the first hemistich concerns the Vala myth: the word phalig├б- тАШboltтАЩ is associated with the Vala myth in two of its three other occurrences (I.62.4, IV.50.5), once of the Vс╣Ыtra myth (VIII.32.25), never of ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa. However, if this is the Vala myth it is somewhat puzzling why the sun is entering the dark, since the Vala myth is usually set at dawn. Perhaps this refers to a version in which the sun is also trapped in the Vala cave.

I supply тАШfoldтАЩ in the temporal abl. expression in p─Бda a, since I would expect an acc. of goal, and p─Б╠Бthas- тАШfoldтАЩ is common with ├бpi тИЪi (I.162.2, II.3.9, III.8.9, VII.47.3). On the other hand, perhaps the abl.(/gen.) t├бmasaс╕е is simply by attraction to the abl. infinitive ├бp─лteс╕е.

As noted earlier, ─Б╠Бdaс╕е is analyzed by Hoffmann as an injunctive in mythological context. Note also that it probably belongs to тИЪdс╣Ы тАШtearтАЩ, not тИЪd─Б, despite ─Б╠Бdo to the latter root in 8a. However, it could technically be underlyingly identical to ─Б╠Бdo, and that p─Бda also contains a div├бс╕е. In that case it would mean тАЬyou took тАжтАЭ

English translation:

тАЬThen the vast, powerful, and immoveable earth and heaven animated you, Indra, to glorious needs, and you did hurl down into the waters, with your mightythunderbolt, the everywhere-spreading and destroying Vс╣Ыtra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two great surfaces that have no wheels, Heaven and Earth, cheered you on at this deed, o Indra:
You put Vr╠еtra to sleep powerfully with your mace, as he was lying upon the streams, (and you put to sleep) the boar [=┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa?].

Jamison Brereton Notes

Hoffmann (191 n. 157) insists that ├бnu тАж madat─Бm must be an impv. This interpr. is of course possible, but I do not see its necessity. He also interprets siс╣гvapaс╕е as a subjunctive. This is also possible, esp. because the other two forms to this redupl. aor. are athematic (s├нс╣гvap). However, again it is not necessary, since redupl. aorists are overwhelmingly thematic, and old athematic ones get thematized (cf. augmented ├бd─лdharat beside d─лdhar).

I have no idea why itтАЩs worth mentioning that Heaven and Earth have no wheels, a seemingly obvious fact, unless to contrast them with Eta┼Ыa and the SunтАЩs wheel in 13b.

In d the easiest thing to do with acc. var─Б╠Бhum тАШboarтАЩ is to take it as an appositive to vс╣Ыtr├бm (much earlier in the hemistich). But the problem, of course, is that Vс╣Ыtra isnтАЩt a boar but a cobra (/serpent). IndraтАЩs boar opponent is Emuс╣гa, and that may be the referent. (See I.61.6-7, where the Vс╣Ыtra and Emuс╣гa myths are told in two successive verses.) However, given that the ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa myth is related here in the two preceding verses (9-10), I think that ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa may be the referent. He does, after all, snort (e.g., I.54.5 ┼Ыvasan├бsya тАж ┼Ы├║с╣гс╣Зasya).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, friend of man, mount the horses whom you cherish, who are fleet as the wind, are easily yoked, and who bear (theri burden) well; you have sharpened the foe-destroying thunderbolt, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, which inspiring (weapon) U┼Ыanas, the son of Kavi, gave you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which inspiring weapon: The weapon was the gift of с╣Ъbhu;and is also attributed to U┼Ыanas

Jamison Brereton

You, o Indra, the manly one driving to the men for helpтАФmount the (horses) of the Wind, the best conveyors, easy to yoke.
What U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya gave to you to provide exhilaration, that decisive, Vr╠еtra-smiting mace had he fashioned.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a contains two ambiguous forms: y─Б╠Бn, which can be either acc. pl.

masc. of the rel. pronoun or pres. act. part., nom. sg. masc., to the root pres. of тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ; ├бvaс╕е, which can be either the 2nd sg. injunc. act. of the them. pres. to тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ or the acc. sg. neut. of ├бvas- тАШaid, helpтАЩ. If we take y─Б╠Бn as a rel. pron., there is the problem that there is no referent for it in the main clause (save for the WindтАЩs horses, which are not likely). Despite the majority of tr., I therefore take it as the participle, with the consequence that ├бvaс╕е is a noun, serving as acc. of goal, rather than a finite verb. (Its accent would be a problem in a non-relative clause.) As it turns out, there are no injunctives to the thematic present of this root: we find either augm.

─Б╠Бvaс╕е (etc.) or subj. ├бv─Бс╕е (etc.); this is an additional, if weak, argument for not taking it as a finite verb.

The adj. mand├нnam тАШexhilaratingтАЩ in c seems semantically far enough from its apparent referent, vajr├бm in d, that Geldner supplies a verb тАЬ(trink)тАЭ to produce a new clause and allow mand├нnam to qualify the expected soma (see the same adj. in 8c).

This is unnecessary. U┼Ыan─Б K─БvyaтАЩs major job is to give Indra the mace (see also V.34.2) and for Indra to reach exhilaration in his company (I.51.11). In our passage it seems as if these are conflated, and the vajra itself is what provides the exhilaration (= the energy to kill Vс╣Ыtra bez. ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa).

Mount Indra, lover of the men thou guardest, the well-yoked horses of the wind, best bearers.
The bolt which Kavya Usana erst gave thee, strong, gladdening, Vrtra-slaying, hath he fashioned.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╕реВрд░рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╣рд░рд┐рддрдГ рд╣рд░рд┐рджреНрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреН рдиреДрдиреН рдиреЗрддреДрдиреН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рд░рд╕рд╣рд░рдгрд╢реАрд▓рд╛рдиреН рд░рд╢реНрдореАрдиреН рд░рдордпрдГ рдЙрдкрд╛рд░рдордпрдГ ред рдПрддрд╢реЛ рди ред рдПрддрд╢ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗ – тАШ рдПрддрд╢реЗрди рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдВ рдЧрдордпрддреБ ’ (рддреИ. рд╕рдВ. рез. рем. рек. рем) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдирд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ ред рдПрддрд╢рд╢реНрдЪ рд░рдерд╕реНрдп рдЪрдХреНрд░рдВ рднрд░рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╣рддреН ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдирд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдирд╛рд╡рд╛ рддрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдирджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдирд╡рддрд┐рдВ рдирд╡рддрд┐рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрддреАрддреНрдп рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдВ рдкрд╛рд░рдВ рддреАрд░рджреЗрд╢рдореН ред рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛ ред рддреАрд░рджреЗрд╢реЗ рдЕрдпрдЬреНрдпреВрдиреН рдЕрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╡рд┐рд╣реАрдирд╛рдиреН рдЕрд╕реБрд░рд╛рджреАрдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрдп рддрддреНрд░ рдХрд░реНрддрдореН рдЕрд╡рд░реНрддрдпрдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдордкрд┐ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рддрд╛рдирдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╡рд░реНрддрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдГ рее рд░рдордпрдГ ред рд▓рдЩрд┐ тАШ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдЩреНрдпреЛрдЧреЗрд╜рдкрд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдбрднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкрд┐ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдВрд╣рд┐рддрдХреЛ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрдп ред тАШрдЕрд╕реБ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдгреЗ ‘ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рд▓реНрдпрдкрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдирд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдореН ред рдиреМрд╡рдпреЛрдзрд░реНрдо’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдпрддреНред рддрд┐рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░рд┐рддрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд┐рддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬStop, S┼лra, your yellow horses, for this Eta┼Ыa, Indra, drags the wheel; having driven those who offer no sacrifices to the opposite bank of the ninety rivers, you compel them (to do) what is to be done.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

S┼лra = Indra, as the sun;

Eta┼Ыa = a horse of the sun; also the name of a с╣Ъс╣гi; ninety rivers = n─Бvy─Бn─Бm, of navigable rivers, or of such as must be crossed by a boat

Jamison Brereton

You brought to a halt the tawny mares of the Sun for men. Eta┼Ыa bore the wheel; (you were) on your own, Indra.
Having cast (it) forth to the far shore of the ninety and nine (rivers), you rolled the non-sacrificers over into the pit.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take nс╣Ы╠Д╠Бn as a gen. pl. (see 1a) in beneficial sense.

For n─Б╠Бy├бm see comm. on VIII.2.28 and Jamison (Hock Fs.).

In c rathy├ас╕е could simply mean тАШcharioteersтАЩ, a parallel gift to the prizes (v─Б╠Бj─Бn). So Witzel Got┼Н.

Griffith

The strong Bay Horses of the Sun thou stayedst: this Etasa drew not the wheel, O Indra.
Casting them forth beyond the ninety rivers thou dravest down into the pit the godless.

Geldner

Du Indra hieltest die Falbinnen des Sonnengottes an, bis ans andere Ufer der neunzig Str├╢me es schleudernd rolltest du die Opferlosen kopf├╝ber in den Abgrund. -

Grassmann

Du liessest ruhn der Sonne starke Rosse, nicht zog der Renner mehr ihr Rad, o Indra, Du schleudertest die B├╢sen in die Grube, sie werfend ├╝ber neunzig grosse Str├╢me.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдордпрдВ рд╕реВрд░реЛ рд╣рд░рд┐рдд рдЗрд╡реИрддрд╢рд╢реНрдЪрдХреНрд░рдВ рдирд╛рдпрдЬреНрдпреВрдиреН рдиреДрдиреН рднрд░рддреНред рдирд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдирд╡рддрд┐рдВ рдирд╡рддрд┐рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдЬрд▓рдЧрдордирд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд┐ рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкрд╛рд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрдпреИрддрд╛рдиреН рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдиреЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрдВ рдЦрдирд┐рддреБрдВ рдХрд░реНрдордХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдВ рдЪрд╛рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдорддреНрд░рд╛рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕рджрд╛ рд░рдордпрдГ рее резрей рее

foundationтАФfor refreshment, for fame, and for liberality.

Vouchsafe us affluence in chariots, founded on horses, for our food and fame and gladness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFamous for affluence, Indra, never may your favour be withdrawn from us; may food ever sustain us; opulent Maghavan, make us possessors of cattle, and may we, most assiduous in your adoration, be happy, together (with our families).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let not your favor wither away from us, o you great in prizes:
refreshments will completely cover (us).
Give us a share in the cows of the stranger, o bounteous one. Might we be your most bounteous feasting companions.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The root affiliation of s├бm тАж varanta is disputed. Most take it as belonging to тИЪvс╣Ы тАШchooseтАЩ (Geldner, Renou [apparently, see below], Witzel Got┼Н); I follow Grassmann and Lubotsky in assigning it to тИЪvс╣Ы тАШcoverтАЩ. Although it is difficult to judge, there are more clear root aor. subjunctive middle forms to тАШcoverтАЩ than to тАШchooseтАЩ (though cf. I.140.13 where varanta does belong to тАШchooseтАЩ and takes ├нс╣гam as object). Moreover, s├бm does not appear to be found with тАШchooseтАЩ, but is at least marginally attested with тАШcoverтАЩ (cf. VIII.17.7 and X.16.7).

The other question about this verb is what is its subject. Geldner takes ├нс╣гaс╕е as the acc. pl. obj. and supplies the singers or rich patrons as subj. (sim. Witzel Got┼Н): тАЬSie bitten sich alle Gen├╝sse (als Lohn) aus.тАЭ Inserting a 3rd ps. subject is a bit awkward in a verse in which the human petitioners are otherwise in the 1st ps. (a asm├бt, c naс╕е, d sy─Бma). Renou takes ├нс╣гaс╕е as the subject, in one of his finer sleights of hand: тАЬPuissent les jouissances-rituelles affluer (-comme-par-choix!),тАЭ where the supposed root verb appears only in the parenthesis and the Sanskrit justification for тАЬaffluerтАЭ is entirely unclear. I take ├нс╣гaс╕е as the subject, with тАШusтАЩ supplied as object: тАЬcompletely cover (us)тАЭ expresses the abundance of refreshments Indra will provide.

Griffith

Never may this thy loving-kindness fail us; mighty in strength, may plenteous food surround us.
Maghavan, make us share the foeman’s cattle: may we be thy most liberal feast companions.

Geldner

Nicht soll diese deine Huld uns fehlen, du Beutereicher. Sie bitten sich alle Gen├╝sse als Lohn aus. Gib uns einen Anteil an den K├╝hen des reichen Patrons, du Gabenreicher! Wir wollen deine freigebigsten Zechgenossen sein!

Grassmann

Nie m├╢g’ uns mangeln diese deine G├╝te; kraftreiche Tr├дnke m├╢gen sich uns mehren, Des Feindes Heerden theil uns zu, o reicher, wir seien deine reichsten Tischgenossen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдорд╣реЛ рдордШрд╡рдЮреНрдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдХреГрдкрдпрд╛ рдпрд╛ рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдордиреНрдорд╛ рд╡рд┐ рджрд╕рддреНрдХрджрд╛рдЪрд┐рдиреНрди рд╡рд┐рдирд╢реНрдпреЗрддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдЬрдирд╛ рдЗрд╖рдГ рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдиреНрддред рдЕрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЧреЛрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рднрдЬ рдпрддреЛ рдордВрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рее резрел рее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдмреБрджреНрдзреАрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреАрд╕рд╛рдареА рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдорд╛рдиреВрди рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердирд╛ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реА. рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЪреЗ рдЬрд╕реЗ рдЧреБрдг, рдХрд░реНрдо, рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд рддрд╕реЗ рдЖрдкрд▓реЗ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рдХрд░реВрди рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд│ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдЖрдирдВрджрд╛рдд рд╕реНрдерд┐рдд рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резрел рее
